\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Computes the trace of a square matrix $\sum_{i=0}^{N-1}a_{ii}$. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
{\footnotesize template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ }\\\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$ T $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_ac742a1d3567f0f56ad6d2196d2960e85}{Determinant}} (const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&A)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Computes the determinant of a square matrix defined by $\sum_{i=0}^{N-1}(-1)^ia_{0i}\det(A_{0i})$ where $A_{0i}$ is the (N-\/1)x(N-\/1) matrix obtained by deleting the 0th row and ith column. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
{\footnotesize template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ }\\\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$ T $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a2427bd1ff44d2875ca7f07c7d047e39f}{Minor}} (const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&A, size\+\_\+t i, size\+\_\+t j)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Computes the (i,j)-\/minor of a square matrix defined by $\det(A_{ij})$ where $A_{ij}$ is the (N-\/1)x(N-\/1) matrix obtained by deleting the ith row and jth column. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
{\footnotesize template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ }\\\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$ T $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a2af21abf09659a8df011d15cf6e48f26}{Cofactor}} (const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&A, size\+\_\+t i, size\+\_\+t j)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Computes the (i,j)-\/cofactor of a square matrix defined by $(-1)^{i+j}\det(A_{ij})$ where $A_{ij}$ is the (N-\/1)x(N-\/1) matrix obtained by deleting the ith row and jth column. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
{\footnotesize template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ }\\\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a47539cd2c0b65666a67821896a450d5a}{Adjugate}} (const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&A)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Computes the NxN adjugate B of a square matrix A defined by $b_{ij}=c_{ji}$ where $c_{ij}$ represents the (i,j)-\/cofactor of A. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
{\footnotesize template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ }\\\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a72988b2b8fec9ebd3f5b9eed64a96f76}{Inverse}} (const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&A)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Computes the NxN inverse $A^{-1}=\frac{1}{\det A}Adj$ of a square matrix A where Adj is the adjugate of A. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$T,M,N,Flags$>$ Linear\+::\+Adjugate (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{A }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes the NxN adjugate B of a square matrix A defined by $b_{ij}=c_{ji}$ where $c_{ij}$ represents the (i,j)-\/cofactor of A. 

If A is not square, an exception is thrown.

\end{DoxyParams}

\index{Linear@{Linear}!Basis@{Basis}}
\index{Basis@{Basis}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Basis()}{Basis()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags = 0$>$ \\
std\+::enable\+\_\+if$<$(M$>$0\&\&N$>$0), \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$T,M,N,Flags$>$ $>$\+::type Linear\+::\+Basis (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{i,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{j }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Creates an MxN basis matrix $A$ where all entries are set to 0 except $a_{ij}=1$. 

If i or j are out of bounds, an exception is thrown.

Example\+: A is the 2x2 matrix \{\{0,1\}, \{0,0\}\} \begin{DoxyVerb}Matrix2d A = Basis<double, 2, 2>(0, 1);
\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em T} & Type \\
\hline
{\em M} & Number of rows \\
\hline
{\em N} & Number of columns \\
\hline
{\em Flags} & Flags to pass to the matrix (default = row major) \\
\hline
{\em i} & Row index \\
\hline
{\em j} & Column index \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
MxN \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_linear_a7fa54b4fd13c37b0296853335bedcabf}\label{namespace_linear_a7fa54b4fd13c37b0296853335bedcabf}} 
\index{Linear@{Linear}!Basis@{Basis}}
\index{Basis@{Basis}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Basis()}{Basis()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , unsigned int Flags = 0$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$T,\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a4895328b97c3a485bb1481f7c4dfee00}{Dynamic}},\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a4895328b97c3a485bb1481f7c4dfee00}{Dynamic}},Flags$>$ Linear\+::\+Basis (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{nrows,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{ncols,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{i,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{j }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Dynamically creates an nrowsxncols basis matrix $A$ where all entries are set to 0 except $a_{ij}=1$. 

If i or j are out of bounds, an exception is thrown.

Example\+: A is the 2x2 matrix \{\{0,1\}, \{0,0\}\} \begin{DoxyVerb}MatrixXd A = Basis<double>(2, 2, 0, 1);
\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}

\hline

\hline
{\em ncols} & Number of columns \\
\hline
{\em i} & Row index \\
\hline
{\em j} & Column index \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
nrowsxncols \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M4, N4, Flags4 $>$ \&}]{br }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Creates the (M1+\+M3)x(N1+\+N2) block matrix. 

\[ \begin{bmatrix} tl & tr \\ bl & br \end{bmatrix}. \] If $M1+M3\ne M2+M4$ or $N1+N2\ne N3+N4$, then an exception is thrown.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a89a3a94b7d8b9a7b36e9f8c98f3a2f88}{Vector}}$<$T,(N==\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a4895328b97c3a485bb1481f7c4dfee00}{Dynamic}}?Dynamic\+:N+1)$>$ Linear\+::\+Char\+Poly (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{A }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes the characteristic polynomial. 

This returns the coefficients as a vector c of length N+1 such that $\det(A-tI)=c_0+c_1t+\dots+c_{N-1}t^{N-1}+c_Nt^N$.

\index{Linear@{Linear}!Cofactor@{Cofactor}}
\index{Cofactor@{Cofactor}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cofactor()}{Cofactor()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$T$>$ Linear\+::\+Cofactor (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{A,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{i,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{j }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes the (i,j)-\/cofactor of a square matrix defined by $(-1)^{i+j}\det(A_{ij})$ where $A_{ij}$ is the (N-\/1)x(N-\/1) matrix obtained by deleting the ith row and jth column. 

If A is not square, an exception is thrown. Likewise if i or j is out-\/of-\/bounds an exception is thrown. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em A} & MxN matrix \\
\hline
{\em i} & Row index \\
\hline
{\em j} & Column index \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}} number 
\end{DoxyReturn}

Computes a basis for the column space of A. 

The column space of a matrix is the set of vectors v such that Ax=v for some vector x.

Computes the (N-\/1)x(N-\/1) companion matrix. 

\[ C = \begin{bmatrix} 0 & 0 & \dots & 0 & -c_0/c_{N-1} \\ 1 & 0 & \dots & 0 & -c_1/c_{N-1} \\ 0 & 1 & \dots & 0 & -c_2/c_{N-1} \\ \vdots & \vdots & \ddots & \vdots & \vdots \\ 0 & 0 & \dots & 1 & -c_{N-2}/c_{N-1} \end{bmatrix} \] such that $\det(C-tI)=c_0/c_{N-1}+c_1/c_{N-1}t+\dots+c_{N-2}/c_{N-1}t^{N-2}+t^{N-1}$.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_linear_a1d7c9f59b6085207a5a193a64513fb0e}\label{namespace_linear_a1d7c9f59b6085207a5a193a64513fb0e}} 
\index{Linear@{Linear}!Cross@{Cross}}
\index{Cross@{Cross}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cross()}{Cross()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags, size\+\_\+t P, size\+\_\+t Q, unsigned int Flags2$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$T,M,N,Flags$>$ Linear\+::\+Cross (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{a,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, P, Q, Flags2 $>$ \&}]{b }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes the cross product of two vectors a and b both of length 3. 

The cross product is defined by \[a\times b = (a_0i+a_1j+a_2k)\times (b_0i+b_1j+b_2k)=(a_1b_2-a_2b_1)i + (a_2b_0-a_0b_2)j + (a_0b_1-a_1b_0)k.\] If either a or b is not a vector, or they aren\textquotesingle{}t length 3, an exception is thrown.

Example\+: c is the column vector \{-\/3,6,-\/3\} \begin{DoxyVerb}Vector3d a = {1, 2, 3};
Vector3d b = {4, 5, 6};
Vector3d c = Cross(a,b);
\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em a} & Row/column vector \\
\hline
{\em b} & Row/column vector \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Column vector if a is a column vector, otherwise row vector. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_linear_a834e1a6349d453345f6c1fd26759edb5}\label{namespace_linear_a834e1a6349d453345f6c1fd26759edb5}}

\index{Linear@{Linear}!Determinant@{Determinant}}
\index{Determinant@{Determinant}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Determinant()}{Determinant()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$T$>$ Linear\+::\+Determinant (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{A }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes the determinant of a square matrix defined by $\sum_{i=0}^{N-1}(-1)^ia_{0i}\det(A_{0i})$ where $A_{0i}$ is the (N-\/1)x(N-\/1) matrix obtained by deleting the 0th row and ith column. 

If A is not square, an exception is thrown. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em A} & MxN matrix \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}} number 
\end{DoxyReturn}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags, size\+\_\+t P, size\+\_\+t Q, unsigned int Flags2$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$T$>$ Linear\+::\+Dot (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{a,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, P, Q, Flags2 $>$ \&}]{b }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes the dot product of two vectors a and b both of size N, $\sum{i=0}^{N-1}\overline{a_i}b_i$. 

If either a or b is not a vector, or they have differing sizes, an exception is thrown.

Example\+: z=1$\ast$3+2$\ast$4=11 \begin{DoxyVerb}Vector2d a = {1, 2};
Vector2d b = {3, 4};
Complexd z = Dot(a,b);
\end{DoxyVerb}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_linear_a498247f6fcf1caa95824099e53ddac04}\label{namespace_linear_a498247f6fcf1caa95824099e53ddac04}} 
\index{Linear@{Linear}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Eigen()}{Eigen()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{struct_linear_1_1_eigenpair}{Eigenpair}}$<$T,N$>$ $>$ Linear\+::\+Eigen (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{A }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Calculates all eigenpairs of A. 

This function handles various cases. First, if the matrix is either upper or lower triangular, then the eigenvalues are simply across the diagonal. Allowing us to pull them directly out of the matrix and use either the Nullspace or Inverse\+Iteration to calculate their corresponding eigenvectors. Second, if the matrix is 2x2, then a easy direct formula exists to calculate the eigenvalues. Namely $(tr(A)\pm\sqrt{tr(A)^2-4det(A)})/2$. Third, if neither of the first two cases handles the matrix, we attempt to calculate the \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_linear_1_1_schur}{Schur}} decomposition of A. If that fails, we resort to calling Wielandt\+Deflation\+Algorithm. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em A} & MxN matrix \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
List of Eigenpairs 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_linear_ab0b3eaf397d0a0b65b7f182c6deaf892}\label{namespace_linear_ab0b3eaf397d0a0b65b7f182c6deaf892}} 
\index{Linear@{Linear}!Eigenvalues@{Eigenvalues}}
\index{Eigenvalues@{Eigenvalues}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Eigenvalues()}{Eigenvalues()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a89a3a94b7d8b9a7b36e9f8c98f3a2f88}{Vector}}$<$T,N$>$ Linear\+::\+Eigenvalues (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{A }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Calculates all eigenvalues of A. 

This function handles various cases. First, if the matrix is either upper or lower triangular, then the eigenvalues are simply across the diagonal. Allowing us to pull them directly out of the matrix and use either the Nullspace or Inverse\+Iteration to calculate their corresponding eigenvectors. Second, if the matrix is 2x2, then a easy direct formula exists to calculate the eigenvalues. Namely $(tr(A)\pm\sqrt{tr(A)^2-4det(A)})/2$. Third, if neither of the first two cases handles the matrix, we attempt to calculate the \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_linear_1_1_schur}{Schur}} decomposition of A. If that fails, we resort to calling Wielandt\+Deflation\+Algorithm.

{\em A} & MxN matrix \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Column vector of eigenvalues. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\index{Exp@{Exp}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Exp()}{Exp()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$T$>$ Linear\+::\+Exp (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$ T $>$ \&}]{z }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Takes a complex number $z$ and computes $e^z$. 

This is done using Euler\textquotesingle{}s formula. Thus $e^z=e^{a+bi}=e^ae^{bi}=e^a(\cos b+i\sin b)$.

\index{Linear@{Linear}!Exp@{Exp}}
\index{Exp@{Exp}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Exp()}{Exp()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$T,M,N,Flags$>$ Linear\+::\+Exp (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$}]{A }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



If $A$ is not square, it computes the MxN \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} $B$ defined by $b_{ij}=e^{a_{ij}}$. 

Otherwise it computes the matrix exponential $e^A=\sum_{k=0}^\infty\frac{1}{k!}A^k$. If $A=VDV^{-1}$ with $D=diag(d_1,\dots,d_N)$ a diagonal matrix, then $e^{A}=Ve^{D}V^{-1}$ and $e^D=diag(e^{d_1},\dots,e^{d_N})$. If no such decomposition can be found, it simply estimates the series upto the first 10 terms. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em A} & MxN \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
MxN \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} 
\end{DoxyReturn}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a35a747d6e3c877b1aeeaad3b1951f8e1}{Row\+Vector}}$<$T,N$>$ $>$ Linear\+::\+Gram\+Schmidt (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a35a747d6e3c877b1aeeaad3b1951f8e1}{Row\+Vector}}$<$ T, N $>$$>$ \&}]{v }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Performs Gram-\/\+Schmidt on a list of row vectors. 

If all vectors don\textquotesingle{}t have the same length, an exception is thrown.

Example\+: vectors is the list of row vectors \{0.\+477,0.\+894\} and \{0.\+894,-\/0.\+477\} \begin{DoxyVerb}RowVector2d v1 = { 1, 2 };
RowVector2d v2 = { 3, 4 };
std::vector<RowVector2d> vectors = { v1, v2 };
vectors = GramSchmidt(vectors);
\end{DoxyVerb}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T $>$ \\

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$T,M,N,Flags$>$ Linear\+::\+Inverse (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{A }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes the NxN inverse $A^{-1}=\frac{1}{\det A}Adj$ of a square matrix A where Adj is the adjugate of A. 

If A is not square or if A is singular, an exception is thrown.

\index{Linear@{Linear}!InverseIteration@{InverseIteration}}
\index{InverseIteration@{InverseIteration}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{InverseIteration()}{InverseIteration()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags, size\+\_\+t P$>$ \\
std\+::enable\+\_\+if$<$(P==N$\vert$$\vert$P==\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a4895328b97c3a485bb1481f7c4dfee00}{Dynamic}}$\vert$$\vert$N==\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a4895328b97c3a485bb1481f7c4dfee00}{Dynamic}}), \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a89a3a94b7d8b9a7b36e9f8c98f3a2f88}{Vector}}$<$T,P$>$ $>$\+::type Linear\+::\+Inverse\+Iteration (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{A,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a89a3a94b7d8b9a7b36e9f8c98f3a2f88}{Vector}}$<$ T, P $>$}]{b0,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$ T $>$}]{mu,  }\item[{unsigned int}]{max\+\_\+iterations }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Performs inverse iteration on A with guess mu. 

Inverse iteration, defined by the sequence $b_{k+1}=\frac{(A-\mu I)^{-1}b_k}{\|(A-\mu I)^{-1}b_k\|}$ is a simple algorithm that computes the eigenvalue of A closest to mu along with it\textquotesingle{}s corresponding eigenvector. Convergence rate depends on how close mu is.

More information\+: \href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inverse_iteration}{\texttt{ https\+://en.\+wikipedia.\+org/wiki/\+Inverse\+\_\+iteration}} 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em A} & MxN matrix \\
\hline
{\em b0} & Initial vector of length P to start the sequence \\
\hline
{\em mu} & Original guess at an eigenvalue \\
\hline
{\em max\+\_\+iterations} & Maximum number of iterations to perform \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Vector v such that $Av\approx\lambda v$ where $\lambda$ is the eigenvalue of A closest to mu 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_linear_a73d90ec869ba15e389a193e093600810}\label{namespace_linear_a73d90ec869ba15e389a193e093600810}}

\[ A\otimes B = \begin{bmatrix} a_{0,0}B & \dots & a_{0,N-1}B \\ \vdots & \ddots & \vdots \\ a_{M-1,0}B & \dots & a_{M-1,N-1}B \end{bmatrix}. \]

\index{Linear@{Linear}!Log@{Log}}
\index{Log@{Log}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Log()}{Log()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/9]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$T$>$ Linear\+::\+Log (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$ T $>$ \&}]{z }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes the principal natural log of a complex number $z$. 

If we use Euler\textquotesingle{}s formula and rewrite $z=re^{\varphi i}$, then $\log z=\log r+\varphi i$. Generally this would be considered a multivalued function as $\log z=\{\log r+(\varphi+2\pi k)i\mid k\in\mathbb{Z}\}$. But we just take the principal natural log, i.\+e., set $k=0$.

(Read more\+: \href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Complex_number\#Complex_logarithm}{\texttt{ https\+://en.\+wikipedia.\+org/wiki/\+Complex\+\_\+number\#\+Complex\+\_\+logarithm}}) 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em z} & \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}} number \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}} number. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_linear_a455548d0b52d70c8789a2c89f1a83abc}\label{namespace_linear_a455548d0b52d70c8789a2c89f1a83abc}}

\index{Log@{Log}!Linear@{Linear}}

\index{Linear@{Linear}!Minor@{Minor}}
\index{Minor@{Minor}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Minor()}{Minor()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$T$>$ Linear\+::\+Minor (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{A,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{i,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{j }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes the (i,j)-\/minor of a square matrix defined by $\det(A_{ij})$ where $A_{ij}$ is the (N-\/1)x(N-\/1) matrix obtained by deleting the ith row and jth column. 

If A is not square, an exception is thrown. Likewise if i or j is out-\/of-\/bounds an exception is thrown.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_linear_ab1a0827063fcbfb3f14c4c1e0c8d4177}\label{namespace_linear_ab1a0827063fcbfb3f14c4c1e0c8d4177}} 
\index{Linear@{Linear}!Norm@{Norm}}
\index{Norm@{Norm}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Norm()}{Norm()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ \\
T Linear\+::\+Norm (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{A,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{p = {\ttfamily 2} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



If $A$ is a vector, it computes the entrywise vector p-\/norm $\left(\sum_{i=0}^{N-1}|a_i|^p\right)^{1/p}$. 

Otherwise it computes the matrix norm $\|A\|_p$. If p=1, it returns $\max_{j=0,\dots,N-1}\sum_{i=0}^{M-1}|a_{ij}|$. If p=2, it returns the largest singular value of $A$. Otherwise an error is returned. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em A} & MxN \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} \\
\hline
{\em p} & Real number (default = 2) \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Real number 
\end{DoxyReturn}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$T$>$ Linear\+::\+Pow (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$ T $>$ \&}]{z,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$ T $>$ \&}]{w }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes the complex number $z^w$. 

This is done using the exponential, $z^w:=e^{w\log z}$. Again this is a multivalued function but we take the principal value.

\index{Linear@{Linear}!Pow@{Pow}}
\index{Pow@{Pow}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Pow()}{Pow()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/4]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags, typename U $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$T,M,N,Flags$>$ Linear\+::\+Pow (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{A,  }\item[{U}]{power }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_linear_af9dec09dae9751ec926b2a2edf9307c3}\label{namespace_linear_af9dec09dae9751ec926b2a2edf9307c3}} 
\index{Linear@{Linear}!Pow@{Pow}}
\index{Pow@{Pow}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Pow()}{Pow()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [3/4]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$T,M,N,Flags$>$ Linear\+::\+Pow (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$}]{A,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$ T $>$}]{power }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



If $A$ is not square, it computes the MxN \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} $B$ defined by $b_{ij}=a_{ij}^{power}$. 

Otherwise it attempts to computes the matrix power $A^{power}$. If $A=VDV^{-1}$ with $D=diag(d_1,\dots,d_N)$ a diagonal matrix, then $A^{power}=VD^{power}V^{-1}$ and $D^{power}=diag(d_1^{power},\dots,d_N^{power})$. If no such decomposition can be found and power is an integer, it multiplies A by itself $\vert$power$\vert$-\/times then taking the inverse if power$<$0. Otherwise it gives up and throws an exception. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em A} & MxN \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
MxN \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_linear_af22418625d431d99d23518aa20613a34}\label{namespace_linear_af22418625d431d99d23518aa20613a34}}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_linear_a08001cdbe10207225ad8a4e77ebe6c4a}\label{namespace_linear_a08001cdbe10207225ad8a4e77ebe6c4a}} 
\index{Linear@{Linear}!PowerIteration@{PowerIteration}}
\index{PowerIteration@{PowerIteration}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{PowerIteration()}{PowerIteration()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags, size\+\_\+t P$>$ \\
std\+::enable\+\_\+if$<$(P==N$\vert$$\vert$P==\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a4895328b97c3a485bb1481f7c4dfee00}{Dynamic}}$\vert$$\vert$N==\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a4895328b97c3a485bb1481f7c4dfee00}{Dynamic}}), \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_linear_1_1_eigenpair}{Eigenpair}}$<$T,P$>$ $>$\+::type Linear\+::\+Power\+Iteration (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{A,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a89a3a94b7d8b9a7b36e9f8c98f3a2f88}{Vector}}$<$ T, P $>$}]{b0,  }\item[{unsigned int}]{max\+\_\+iterations }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Performs power iteration on A. 

Power iteration, defined by the sequence $b_{k+1}=\frac{Ab_k}{\|Ab_k\|}$ is a simple algorithm that computes the greatest (in magnitude) eigenvalue of A along with it\textquotesingle{}s corresponding eigenvector. Convergence is often slow.

More information\+: \href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_iteration}{\texttt{ https\+://en.\+wikipedia.\+org/wiki/\+Power\+\_\+iteration}} 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em A} & MxN matrix \\
\hline
{\em b0} & Initial vector of length P to start the sequence. \\
\hline
{\em max\+\_\+iterations} & Maximum number of iterations to perform \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Pair $(\lambda,v)$ such that $Av\approx \lambda v$ 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_linear_a77d94e43e14353375a9623891abf7674}\label{namespace_linear_a77d94e43e14353375a9623891abf7674}} 
\index{Linear@{Linear}!Proj@{Proj}}
\index{Proj@{Proj}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Proj()}{Proj()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags, size\+\_\+t P, size\+\_\+t Q, unsigned int Flags2$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$T,P,Q,Flags2$>$ Linear\+::\+Proj (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{v,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, P, Q, Flags2 $>$ \&}]{onto }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes the vector projection $\proj_{onto}v = \frac{Dot(onto,v)}{Dot(onto,onto)}onto$. 

If onto is the zero vector, by definition this function will return the zero vector. If either v or onto is not a vector, or they have different lengths, an exception is thrown.

Example\+: w is the column vector \{2,0\} \begin{DoxyVerb}Vector2d v = {2, 2};
Vector2d onto = {1, 0};
Vector2d w = Proj(v,onto);
\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em v} & Row/column vector \\
\hline
{\em onto} & Row/column vector \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Column vector if onto is a column vector, otherwise row vector. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$T,M,N,Flags$>$ Linear\+::\+Random (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$ T $>$}]{min = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$T$>$(0.0)},  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$ T $>$}]{max = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$T$>$(1.0)} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Creates an MxN random matrix $A$ where all entries are randomly determined between min and max. 

If $min=a+bi$ and $max=c+di$, then each entry of $A$ will be of the form $x+iy$ where $a\le x\le c$ and $b\le y\le d$.

\index{Linear@{Linear}!Sign@{Sign}}
\index{Sign@{Sign}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Sign()}{Sign()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$T$>$ Linear\+::\+Sign (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$ T $>$ \&}]{z }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Takes a complex number $z$ and computes $sgn(z)$. 

If $z$ is real and if $z>0$ it returns $1$. If $z$ is real and $z=0$ it returns $0$. Otherwise if $z$ is real it returns $-1$. If $z$ is not real, it returns $\frac{z}{|z|}$. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em z} & \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}} number. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}} number. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\index{Linear@{Linear}!Solve@{Solve}}
\index{Solve@{Solve}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Solve()}{Solve()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags, size\+\_\+t P$>$ \\
std\+::enable\+\_\+if$<$(M==P$\vert$$\vert$P==\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a4895328b97c3a485bb1481f7c4dfee00}{Dynamic}}$\vert$$\vert$M==\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a4895328b97c3a485bb1481f7c4dfee00}{Dynamic}}), \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a89a3a94b7d8b9a7b36e9f8c98f3a2f88}{Vector}}$<$T,N$>$ $>$\+::type Linear\+::\+Solve (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{A,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a89a3a94b7d8b9a7b36e9f8c98f3a2f88}{Vector}}$<$ T, P $>$ \&}]{b }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Solves the matrix equation Ax=b for x. 

This functions breaks into various cases.
\begin{DoxyEnumerate}
\item If A is square we have 2 special cases. a. If A is invertible, then $x=A^{-1}b$. b. If A is upper triangular or lower triangular, then we can use forward/backward subsitution to solve.
\item If those two cases don\textquotesingle{}t hold, we employ Guassian elimination. If M != P, an exception is thrown. If there is no solution, an exception is thrown. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em A} & MxN matrix \\
\hline
{\em b} & Vector of length P \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Vector of length N 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\end{DoxyEnumerate}\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_linear_a9c410068fb3174ea9cb431fb19bbaf8d}\label{namespace_linear_a9c410068fb3174ea9cb431fb19bbaf8d}} 
\index{Linear@{Linear}!Sqrt@{Sqrt}}
\index{Sqrt@{Sqrt}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Sqrt()}{Sqrt()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$T$>$ Linear\+::\+Sqrt (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}}$<$ T $>$ \&}]{z }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Takes a complex number $z=a+bi$ and computes it\textquotesingle{}s principal square root $\sqrt{z}=\gamma+\delta i$, where $\gamma=\sqrt{\frac{a+|z|}{2}}$ and $\delta=(sgn b)\sqrt{\frac{-a+|z|}{2}}$. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em z} & \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}} number. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_complex}{Complex}} number. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_linear_a779e9a357b5de38d43695e262396b98e}\label{namespace_linear_a779e9a357b5de38d43695e262396b98e}} 
\index{Linear@{Linear}!WielandtDeflationAlgorithm@{WielandtDeflationAlgorithm}}
\index{WielandtDeflationAlgorithm@{WielandtDeflationAlgorithm}!Linear@{Linear}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{WielandtDeflationAlgorithm()}{WielandtDeflationAlgorithm()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t M, size\+\_\+t N, unsigned int Flags$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_linear_a89a3a94b7d8b9a7b36e9f8c98f3a2f88}{Vector}}$<$T,N$>$ Linear\+::\+Wielandt\+Deflation\+Algorithm (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_linear_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}$<$ T, M, N, Flags $>$ \&}]{A,  }\item[{unsigned int}]{max\+\_\+iterations = {\ttfamily 100} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Performs a combination of deflation and power iteration to get every eigenpair of A Since power iteration returns the largest eigenvalue, if we want to compute the eigenvalues we need to use deflation. 

The general idea is that once an eigenvalue is calculated, we reduce A to a slightly smaller matrix which has the same eigenvalues except removing the one we just calculated. Repeating this process eventually computes all eigenvalues. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em A} & MxN matrix \\
\hline
{\em max\+\_\+iterations} & Maximum number of iterations to perform for each call of Power\+Iteration \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Column vector of eigenvalues. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
